<div id="review_1507916148" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1507916148" />
    <a title="Nouf *LostinFantasy*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33795465-nouf-lostinfantasy"><img alt="Nouf *LostinFantasy*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1480352284p2/33795465.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1507916148?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nouf *LostinFantasy*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nouf *LostinFantasy*" href="/user/show/33795465-nouf-lostinfantasy">Nouf *LostinFantasy*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33795465-nouf-lostinfantasy?shelf=fantasy-sci-fi">fantasy-sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33795465-nouf-lostinfantasy?shelf=favorite-characters">favorite-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33795465-nouf-lostinfantasy?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33795465-nouf-lostinfantasy?shelf=time-travel">time-travel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33795465-nouf-lostinfantasy?shelf=i-ship-it">i-ship-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33795465-nouf-lostinfantasy?shelf=friendship">friendship</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33795465-nouf-lostinfantasy?shelf=pov-switching">pov-switching</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33795465-nouf-lostinfantasy?shelf=family">family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33795465-nouf-lostinfantasy?shelf=jan-2017-release">jan-2017-release</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33795465-nouf-lostinfantasy?shelf=2017-release">2017-release</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1507916148" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13278399905491964208"><b> Actual Rating:</b> exactly 4/5.<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"How sad for them, she thought, that they had grown up without any thorns with which to protect themselves."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>It's kind of hard to write a review for a sequel when I never did for the first one. (For a great review of book one, you can read my friend Shahad's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1822908877' rel='nofollow noopener'>review of Passenger.</a> So well put, and mirrored my thoughts on it exactly!) <br/><br/>But I am so happy to say that Wayfarer turned out to be <b>a wonderful conclusion</b> to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20983362.Passenger__Passenger___1_' title='Passenger (Passenger, #1) by Alexandra Bracken' rel='nofollow noopener'>Passenger</a>. And that ending...<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1484704252ra/21743641.gif' width='280' height='320' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>There is so much</span>
  <span id="freeText13278399905491964208" style="display:none"><b> Actual Rating:</b> exactly 4/5.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"How sad for them, she thought, that they had grown up without any thorns with which to protect themselves."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>It's kind of hard to write a review for a sequel when I never did for the first one. (For a great review of book one, you can read my friend Shahad's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1822908877" rel="nofollow noopener">review of Passenger.</a> So well put, and mirrored my thoughts on it exactly!) <br><br>But I am so happy to say that Wayfarer turned out to be <b>a wonderful conclusion</b> to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20983362.Passenger__Passenger___1_" title="Passenger (Passenger, #1) by Alexandra Bracken" rel="nofollow noopener">Passenger</a>. And that ending...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1484704252ra/21743641.gif" width="280" height="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There is so much I love about this duology. Alexandra Bracken wrote such a detailed and <b>wonderfully emotional story</b>. It's as much about time travel as it is about family-ties and heartbreak, love and revenge.<br> <br>((BTW, if you've read Passenger but have trouble remembering the events-- and yeah how the time travel works exactly -- there's a really cool and very helpful recap! <br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://static1.squarespace.com/static/57d478de414fb51a88afb5c3/t/5863fce1cd0f689594067006/1482947821967/wayfarer+%281%29.png">https://static1.squarespace.com/stati...</a>))<br><br>I love time travel stories! And <b>I love the explanation for the characters' time traveling ability here.</b> We get a satisfying idea of how it works in the first book. But in this sequel, <b>the origins behind the astrolabe and the four families is revealed.</b> And the war between the travelers intensifies as they all hunt after the astrolabe. There's the Thorns on one side, Rose on another, Etta, and Nicholas, Cyrus Ironwood, the Shadows and an old sinister threat they never saw coming. Every single one has their own agenda and reason for it.<br><br>I loved the world-traveling to different points in history that Etta and Nicholas took in the first book. There's even more traveling here! But better yet, in this book, <b>the travelers' actions actually severely impact and shift world events</b> as a result of everyone fighting for their own version of the timeline. And so, Etta and Nicholas are each faced with hard questions and choices, and not one easy option. So, <b>the plot is definitely exciting!</b> <br><br>Before I talk about the wonderful characters and relationships in this book, I'm going to mention <b>the writing - or rather its pace.</b> The writing is beautiful -- but, in other ways, because of the slow pace, <b>it's also the book's biggest flaw.</b> This book is definitely an improvement on Passenger in terms on pacing, but <b>it still moves a bit slowly at some points</b> with the long descriptions, and also too-long inner monologues every time a character decides on something new. Sometimes you want things to move just a bit faster. Especially, Nicholas and Sophia's journey. I found Etta's parts moving along quicker. <br><br>But it's worth it to be patient because we get great character development and there's enough action, especially during that explosive climactic part. <br>Still, could have been 50 pages shorter or more, maybe.<br><br><u>(If you haven't read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20983362.Passenger__Passenger___1_" title="Passenger (Passenger, #1) by Alexandra Bracken" rel="nofollow noopener">Passenger</a> yet, below are a couple of big spoilers for the <b>first</b> book. But don't worry, no big spoilers for Wayfarer).</u><br><br><br>This time, <b>Etta</b> and <b>Nicholas</b> are separated for most of the book, (after the final events in Passenger took Etta away from him). <br>And while I love their romance and partnership and waited for their reunion, that didn't bother me. It gave opportunity for each to move the same story forward with their own journey - Etta meets <b>her father, Henry Hemlock</b>, leader of the Thorns. And Nicholas gets caught up in a deadly deal while trying to find Etta. <br><br>But the best part about this were <b>
  <u>the new partnerships</u>
</b> and character dynamics this provided! And <b>amazing character development</b> for everyone! I wasn't a fan of <b>Sophia</b> in the first book, but in this one, she is a lot more fleshed out and sympathetic, and so badass! <b>She and Nicholas made awesome from-hate-to-friendship partners.</b><br>It provided some funny moments: <br><blockquote>
  <b>He was yanked back by his collar before he could swim closer.<br>"Would you stop making eyes at that bloody ship? It’s a <i>siege</i>,” Sophia grated at him. “If they catch us, they won’t just kill us; they’ll make a whole show of it. Use our decapitated bodies to boost morale.”<br><i>Right. Yes. Siege.</i></b>
</blockquote><br>They go from despising each other and death-threats to being partners who could relate, and friends who become very protective of each other. <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>As much as Etta was his heart’s helpmate, Sophia was the sword at his side on the expedition he undertook now.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote> <br>A new character <b>Li Min</b> - a fellow traveler and female pirate - joins and helps them too. She has a heavy and dark past, but she's a great ally to Sophia and Nicholas. And there's even a bit of romance between her and Sophia. And though it's subtle, it works very well, showing a bit more of Sophia's softer side.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Nicholas wondered briefly if it was his destiny to be surrounded by women possessing varying degrees of murderous intent.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>And <b>Etta gets to know her father</b>, Henry Hemlock, who she's never met, and his side of the traveler family, which make up "The Thorns". And it leads her to learn more about her mother, <b>Rose</b>, and her secrets. <br>(Rose is, btw, an amazingly complex anti-herione that deserves more page time --and even her own book).<br><br>But also she meets Nicholas's spoiled and carefree half-brother, <b>Julian Ironwood</b> who (as was hinted at the end of Passenger) is <i>not</i> dead, and turns out to be a very fun addition to the story! And Etta gets stuck with him on her side of things, and they make a hilarious mismatched pair!<br><blockquote>
  <b>"You’re rather handy, Linden-Hemlock-Spencer,” he said. “That was some brilliant teamwork, if I do say so myself.” <br>"I’m not sure you know what that word means,” Etta managed, her teeth clenched. <br>“You’re the brawn, I’m the brains, kiddo,” he told her. “You don’t need my help with this.”</b>
</blockquote><br>And some more later - I loved this line:<br><blockquote>
  <b>She blinked. “That was… surprisingly useful.” <br>"As I like to say, always aim to disappoint in life,” Julian said. “That way you’ll never fail to be a delightful surprise when you don’t.” </b>
</blockquote><br>And, like with Sophia, there's some great character development for Julian!<br><br>But safe to say - absolutely <b>no love triangles in this!</b> Etta and Nicholas's romantic arc is just as strong even with them apart for so long. <br>But the <b>family dynamics and friendships are just as impactful</b> in this book which was my favorite part.<br><br>I do wish that the characters that were separated for most of the book and only met near the end had more scenes together - like Henry and Rose (can I get their love story please - I need that special Target edition with their novella!), Nicholas and Julian (I would have liked more resolution there), and a little more of Sophia and Nicholas after everything. But I just want more of these characters because they were all so likable and complex and just wonderful! <br><br><b>Overall, I'm happy with this book and conclusion to the story.</b> And I would love for novellas to start appearing showing us what happens next to the characters and more of their journeys! And even if not - the ending of this book was perfect enough! <br><br>And if you're hesitant to read this because Passenger felt a bit slow-paced then just remember the fun parts of that book (when it started to pick up with the time-traveling), because this book has <i>a lot</i> more of that, and just overall more surprises.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13278399905491964208" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1572097882" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1572097882" />
    <a title="rachel ☾" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17290119-rachel"><img alt="rachel ☾" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591333266p2/17290119.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1572097882?book_show_action=true">Mar 06, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="rachel ☾" class="user" itemprop="url" name="rachel ☾" href="/user/show/17290119-rachel">rachel ☾</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781460752050" href="/book/show/31306288-wayfarer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17290119-rachel?shelf=rep-bipoc">rep-bipoc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17290119-rachel?shelf=2-star">2-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17290119-rachel?shelf=young-adult-lit">young-adult-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1572097882" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16756540322594718147"><i>This review contains spoilers.<br/><br/>Wayfarer</i> was a long, arduous read that did not live up to the potential established in <i>Passenger</i>. Like most readers, I had massive problems with the writing style and pacing of this sequel. Bracken has the unfortunate habit of picking up random tangents and running with them for several pages at a time. It was infuriating, to say the least. We would be forced to dilly-dally around the main plotline for entire chapters as the characters wasted time doing goodness kno</span>
  <span id="freeText16756540322594718147" style="display:none"><i>This review contains spoilers.<br /><br />Wayfarer</i> was a long, arduous read that did not live up to the potential established in <i>Passenger</i>. Like most readers, I had massive problems with the writing style and pacing of this sequel. Bracken has the unfortunate habit of picking up random tangents and running with them for several pages at a time. It was infuriating, to say the least. We would be forced to dilly-dally around the main plotline for entire chapters as the characters wasted time doing goodness knows what for goodness know what reason. The book as a whole could easily have been at least 150 shorter if these scenes and repetitive passages in Nicholas’s chapters had been cut down.<br /><br />The characters were another sore spot. Henry was the only character that I genuinely enjoyed. Although looking back, I do have to say that I admire Sophia’s ‘take no shit’ attitude and for being the most rational character in the entire book by far. Unfortunately, the main characters were nothing like I remembered them to be from the first book, especially Nicholas. He did nothing but whinge and whine for the entire book. He used his grief to excuse his poor choices and to a certain extent, I can understand that but damn, he was an idiot for the majority of the books and so self-pitying that it drove me bonkers. Etta was also off. She had literally no personality and I felt like she was oddly absent from the main storyline for the most part. <br /><br />The romance was also poorly written. Etta and Nicholas had no chemistry. Their entire relationship in this book relied on the leftover feels of the one romantic scene in <i>Passenger</i>. No effort was made to develop or deepen their relationship and I was just not feeling it, even if I shipped it in the first book. I needed more. I did like that it had a lot of diverse elements without ramming its theme down our throats. Sophia’s romance was a little forced but it was worth the effort and I liked how seamlessly a gay couple was slipped into the story as well. <br /><br /><i>Wayfarer</i> was very plot-focused but I struggled to keep track of everything that was happening. The entire Belladonna plotline left me clueless. I had no idea what was happening and even now, I do not understand what Shadows are meant to be. I don’t know if I fell asleep at that point or what, all I know is that they stole kids to become assassins or something like that? They were randomly just always there, attacking people, and somehow Nicholas could always injury or kill them, even when he was dying. It was too much for me. It felt unneeded, confusing and plot hole-ish. It also did not help that Nicholas was acting like a clueless rookie. He made stupid decision after stupid decision and drove me insane with frustration. I don’t understand who would trust an Ironwood at this point? It seems such a moronic move to make and why oh why would you make a freaking deal with a witch with such sloppy wording? Everyone know that you have to be hella specific when you make a binding contract with someone. You can always find a loophole and you never, ever promise to do a favour for them in return <i>and not specify when or what that favour is</i>! That is just being dumb. There is no other way to describe it. <br /><br />Also, I desperately need to talk about the ending. Umm, what was that meant to be? I hated it. I was proud of Nicholas for making the decision he did. Screw everyone’s personal motives, he knew he had to put the collective good first and just restore the timeline… and then things went to hell. What was he thinking? I get going into the future to see/be with Etta. I get that and even expected that to happen… but the rest? I was so, so confused. He just decided to open all the passages again, consequences be damned? I cannot wrap up my head around that. It seems like such a stupid thing to do to me. Is that not the reason everything went to hell in the first place? Also, I really, really, really wanted her mum to be evil so that ‘twist’ ruined that for me. <br /><br /><b>Overall?</b><br /><br /><i>Wayfarer</i> was too long, too boring and too poorly constructed for me to enjoy it. I did like some of the historical scenes - the history nerd in my fangirled over Nicholas II - and Henry but I did not enjoy the as a whole much at all. The writing style was dense. The pacing was slow. The characters were unlikable and their relationship lost all its shippy-ness. I was just disappointed by too many elements of this series finale to be satisfied.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16756540322594718147" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2444528936" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2444528936" />
    <a title="Camille ☼" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25663885-camille"><img alt="Camille ☼" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530652209p2/25663885.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2444528936?book_show_action=true">Jul 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Camille ☼" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Camille ☼" href="/user/show/25663885-camille">Camille ☼</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2444528936" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11936850710113520304">This book was, in my opinion, a lot better than the first one. It was not perfect, it got a little messy and confusing at some point but the characters and the worldbuilding really stood out in this book. In this one, we are following the events that follow the separation of Nicholas and Etta at the end of the first book. <br/><br/>I have to admit one thing. I didn't care much for Etta's story most of the book even though I loved the places she visited. <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ Russia and the Romanov !! <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoi</a></span></span>
  <span id="freeText11936850710113520304" style="display:none">This book was, in my opinion, a lot better than the first one. It was not perfect, it got a little messy and confusing at some point but the characters and the worldbuilding really stood out in this book. In this one, we are following the events that follow the separation of Nicholas and Etta at the end of the first book. <br /><br />I have to admit one thing. I didn't care much for Etta's story most of the book even though I loved the places she visited. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Russia and the Romanov !! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Not that I don't like her character or didn't appreciate what she did or what happened around her. The pace and the action in her story though were very limited in comparaison to Nicholas and Sophia's own escape. A lot more action, adventure and humour on their side. I will never express enough how much I loved their part in this story and the develoment of these two characters and their relationship. Nicholas and his kindness, honour and naïvety, Sophia with her sass, her wildness and her own special way of caring for others, Li Min and her mysterious talents an dher wisdom. They were the ultimate trio. I was enthralled in their adventures and the growing of their relationship. Nicholas's protectiveness towards the girls and the girls' own fierce protectiveness towards Nicholas. They loved each other so much. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ And let me not start on Li Min and Sophia's relationship omg  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Etta's story were somewhat duller and even Julian's sparkling personality was not really enough. <br /><br />Nearing the end of the story, I will admit that it became confusing to me and it became a little less interesting to me than the first 70% of the book (usually it's the contrary that happens) but I was still extremely satisfied with the ending and that is something I did not really see coming so that was good. <br /><br />For anyone who read the first book and was wondering whether or nto it's worth it to continue I would say YES. <br /><br />————<br /><br />I gave three stars to the first book of this series and I remember having kind of a mixed opinion. I am rather surprised by how excited I am to read this. There was something about the worldbuilding and the jumping from one period to another that I just really liked and I think time made me forget what I didn't like so I just remember the good things. Meaning Nicholas.</span>

<div id="review_2137377407" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2137377407" />
    <a title="Sharon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23218431-sharon"><img alt="Sharon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1563502369p2/23218431.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2137377407?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sharon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sharon" href="/user/show/23218431-sharon">Sharon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=get-your-shit-together">get-your-shit-together</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=3-stars">3-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=yuck-time-skip">yuck-time-skip</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=and-the-plot-thickens">and-the-plot-thickens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=time-traveling">time-traveling</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2137377407" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17007932086161105913">Conflicted. <br/><br/>In no particular order, the thoughts that have been running through my head while reading this are:<br/>1. The last violin-playing scene that occurred in this book – beautiful. Everything about it was beautiful.<br/>2. It’s kinda awesome that the emotions evoked in this book were so strong. Literally, I have both loved <i>and</i> hated each one of the main characters at one point or another. They are all so flawed. Except for maybe Alice. She has the purest soul ever.<br/>3. Speaking of characters who I l</span>
  <span id="freeText17007932086161105913" style="display:none">Conflicted. <br /><br />In no particular order, the thoughts that have been running through my head while reading this are:<br />1. The last violin-playing scene that occurred in this book – beautiful. Everything about it was beautiful.<br />2. It’s kinda awesome that the emotions evoked in this book were so strong. Literally, I have both loved <i>and</i> hated each one of the main characters at one point or another. They are all so flawed. Except for maybe Alice. She has the purest soul ever.<br />3. Speaking of characters who I love and hate – Sophia’s character development is on pointtttt. I literally hated her guts in the 1st book, and got annoyed with her here and there in this 2nd book. However, I genuinely love learning more about her character, understanding better why she is the way she is. She’s such a fighter and I love it. One particular scene of hers has brought the first tears I have shed for this series. <br />4. I love Sophia and Nicholas’ growing respect for each other and friendship here. They seriously were there for each other.<br />5. Li Min is a badass. A debatable character, but still, a badass. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Also, I ship her romance with Sophia. I would have wanted to see them at the end again, especially reunited. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />6. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Julian <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> is pretty funny. I would have liked to see more character developments because he clearly is capable of being nice and moral. I also would have liked to see more of him and Nicholas interacting.<br />7. WTF. Took forever for the reunion scene.<br />8. It was a bit annoying how Nicholas was chasing after Etta the whole book, while she didn’t even think to go after him. I mean I get she thought he was coming for her (although she literally disappeared out of nowhere, so how would she know that he knew that she wasn’t dead or somewhere else?), and she was very much overwhelmed by the discoveries she was making at the time. But come on, did she stop to think maybe he was stuck in the desert? Or captured by one of the many dangerous players in this book? He could have been in trouble, but she did not think to go back for him, while she was traveling around. She obviously missed him, but it was weird to see how she didn’t actively think of any actions to get them reunited again, while he, on the other hand, was solely focusing on that for most of the book.<br />9. Henry. He seems sweet. He still confuses me and is vaguely fishy to me in every scene. However, he also seems super caring? So I was conflicted on whether or not to trust him throughout the book. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[In the end, I approve. I love seeing him being a warm father figure for Etta. And I find his interactions with Rose to be captivating. My heart truly hurt for them. I hoped they ended up together, despite the time that passed. Furthermore, the violin-playing scenes – both of them – where Henry was watching Etta proudly – loved it. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />10. Bracken has done a wonderful job showing the dual sides of Rose. She is truly someone I love and hate. Hate because why did she have to make it so confusing and complicated? And why was she so cold to her daughter when it wasn’t really necessary? Ah, but it sorta makes sense by the end of the book. I find her actions understandable, even though I don’t think she always took the best approach. I actually end up really feeling for her character. She seemed like such a robot for most of the series. Like a myth figure that everyone seems to have heard of. However, we get a glimpse of her real struggle, her humanity, and the constant state of paranoia that she had to live in.<br />11. I love-hate the ending. It’s kinda satisfying, but not entirely. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I think the problem was the long time skip. One year, really? I mean I get that Nicholas had to first of all, gain courage to go on this mission. And second, he had to sort out the details, find the item of the future. Also, he decided to open up other paths while he was at it and found certain people. I’m just not a big fan of time skips. Also, while it is awesome to see Nicholas morally struggle with using his new power, I feel like along with the moral issue, Nicholas is also struggling with cowardice and facing POSSIBLE disappointment, in case the mission didn’t work. And I’m like, really, you spent weeksssss thinking on using the power or not, while getting gloomy and focusing on the ship? I completely understand his hesitation – as a good person SHOULD struggle with such a big power. I just hated that it took THAT long.<br /><br />The concert scene is truly, truly beautiful. I love how we got see Rose, Henry, AND Nicholas. I would have liked to see Etta actually reunite and talk with her parents again, but it’s nice to see everything ending with the idea that she and Nicholas are going to travel together and establish rules together and create a “peaceful, lawful” society for the time-traveling. <br /><br />It would have been awesome to see a reunion scene with all their friends, but I’m still appreciative that it’s implied that Nicholas and Etta would eventually get there.<br /><br />The Rose epilogue is interesting. It does somewhat show more into Rose’s mind, and I like that her own daughter from the future reassures her about the future. That also may or may not be another reason why Rose focused so much of the responsibilities on Etta in the first book. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>3 stars</b>. Lots of emotions – good and bad. Great characters, interesting character developments. I love the different relationships and friendships we see in this book.<br /><br /><u>Things that you might want to know <b>(WARNING: Spoilers below)</b></u><br />Is there a happy/satisfying ending? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Technically happy. More spoiler-y details in the next spoiler. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[No good, important character died, so happy there (cheers to that). And reunions so happy there. There is a time skip to get to that happy ending so made it a bit gloomy at times. And bumps to work out still. But generally happy. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Love triangle? Cheating? Angst level? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[No, no technical cheating, medium-high.<br /><br />There was this one line, where during a physical separation from Etta, Nicholas thinks something along the lines of going back to routine of work, and he says “Everything had a rhythm, he realized; a recognizable ebb and flow. Love, separation. Work, rest. Pain, rum.” I can’t tell if he’s saying that more as a general saying, or he specifically refers to himself. And I can’t tell if “Love, separation” part of the routine meant he had sex with other girls during this physical separation. He did mention in the 1st book that before he met Etta, he has had sex with several girls before, and he always knew when to leave and continued on with his next trip. So it might mean he’s doing that again? <br /><br />But at the same time, he’s so lovesick for Etta at this time, so did he really? <br /><br />So I’m confused. <br /><br />It’s a vague sentence that I’m not sure if should be taken literally or not. <br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Tears-worthy? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Some tearful moments. Not a too depressing book though. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Humor? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Some funny bantering/dialogue, but in general, no. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Favorite scene? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Seeing Sophia step up her game. Seeing Sophia and Nicholas’ friendship develop. Seeing Sophia and Li Min bond. Seeing any violin-playing scene (because they were always so touching).  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />What age level would be appropriate? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Teenagers and up. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('+qvOaoGC1Wa5urbXFPhI6zGsu0z1omNwFfJWl+D0Y0tBL/8KHmC94VnWTdurWw26u09imz9C91lI+JQ7+vc3WQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('iBZ1UR2SrwkK03XPIb9rmB+Fyyf1medIK0GCYzo59hczkkQxgnDHjuq/jsOeHC7JlWYS8D95c2F2S0DPIDqiBQ==')})
  }
